The Elements of Diagnosis 187

— Song Guobin

There are three essentials to diagnosing diseases: precise examination, prudent prescription, and detailed explanation.

(1) Examination

To obtain an accurate diagnosis and a symptomatic prescription, a legal examination is indispensable. Therefore, the examination should be precise and thorough, thoughtful and clear, have unique insights, and a certain procedure.

A. Precise Examination

The first time a patient is examined, a precise observation should be made. If there is any negligence, it will be too late to regret it. If the diagnosis is inaccurate and the medication is wrongly prescribed, the patient will be in danger. The doctor will lose credibility and ruin his reputation. Both parties will suffer.

B. Thorough Examination

When examining a disease, it is not only necessary to diagnose the disease, but also to understand the patient's level of resistance. Therefore, the examination must be detailed and thorough, and avoid exaggeration, emptiness, negligence, and haste. Today's doctors who can complete an examination in five minutes, their lack of thoroughness is obvious.

C. Examination with Unique Insights

For chronic diseases that have been diagnosed and treated by many doctors, do not easily rely on the diagnoses of others without personally examining them. Even if the previous doctor's diagnosis was not wrong, the time may have changed or the current situation may not be consistent. Therefore, the examination must have unique insights.

D. Organized Examination

The doctor should first allow the patient to describe their history and listen patiently. There are three benefits to this: (1) It can add a line of light to the diagnosis. (2) The patient gets mental comfort because the doctor expresses sympathy. (3) The patient increases their faith in the doctor. Then personally ask questions to supplement the patient's incomplete statement. Finally, conduct a physical examination. Physical examination is sometimes particularly difficult. Ordinary patients are accustomed to the simplicity of pulse diagnosis in traditional medicine and are afraid of the detailed examination of modern doctors. The doctor should explain this well. If rejected, then also refuse to prescribe. However, special caution must be taken in the physical examination of women. The presence of a third person is sometimes really necessary. The world is dangerous, and people are cunning. False accusations and framing often occur. To avoid criticism and protect your reputation, you must be cautious.

E. Deliberate and Discriminating Examination

After the examination is completed, the symptoms should be collected, repeatedly studied, the causes of the disease deduced, and an accurate diagnosis sought. If the symptoms are not complete, it is not appropriate to be arbitrary. It is wise to tell the patient directly. Those young and inexperienced doctors are eager for vanity and pretend to know what they do not know, and the result is often incorrect. Therefore, the examination should be thoughtful.

(2) Prescription

The purpose of the doctor's examination and the patient's invitation is nothing more than a prescription, as a tool to attack the disease demon. However, prescriptions do not only rely on medicines. Sometimes dietary restrictions, guidance on hygiene conditions, or correction of the patient's temperament can also have a considerable effect. The common misconception that a prescription is a drug prescription is wrong.

If a prescription needs to be written, then

(1) You must be bold and careful, and examine in detail. Therefore, when prescribing, you should prohibit others from talking and consulting, so as to avoid mistakes. For children: (A) Do not use weight. (B) Make the medicine easy to take.

(2) The handwriting must be clear to avoid errors when dispensing and causing a major mistake. The signature should also not be too cursive so that the pharmacy can easily inquire when there are doubts. After the prescription is completed, it should be read again to avoid any mistakes.

(3) There must be a possibility of implementation. For example, prescribing expensive drugs for poor patients is not only difficult to implement in practice, but also makes the patient feel disappointed.

(3) Prescription Explanation

After the doctor has carefully considered and written a precise prescription in neat handwriting, he should also write detailed instructions on how to take the medicine in Chinese. Then, explain it to the patient or the female caregiver again and again, striving for clarity. However, female caregivers often think they are smart and do not pay attention to the investigation.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 188

— Cheng Hanzhang

Thirteen: Paratyphoid Fever

(Paratyphus; Paratyphoid fever)

Q: What is paratyphoid fever?

A: Paratyphoid fever is very similar to typhoid fever (enteric fever), but the symptoms are milder.

Q: How does paratyphoid fever start?

A: It is also caused by pathogenic bacteria entering the intestine.

Q: Are the pathogenic bacteria the same as the pathogenic bacteria of typhoid fever?

A: No. They are several other bacteria, collectively called paratyphoid bacilli. (Bacillus Paratyphosus)

Q: How many types of paratyphoid bacilli are there?

A: The A and B types that have been discovered now are called paratyphoid bacilli type A and type B.

Q: Where do these bacteria parasitize?

A: They parasitize in pigs, cattle, cats, oysters, milk, fruits, etc. It is also caused by eating carelessly and mixing these foods into the body.

Page 16

Q: What are the symptoms when paratyphoid fever occurs?

A: Generally, there are two types of symptoms when the disease occurs. One is the typhoid fever type; the other is the gastroenteritis type.

Q: What are the symptoms of the typhoid fever type?

A: The course of symptoms of this type is similar to that of typhoid fever; but what is unique is that the onset is relatively acute at the beginning, often accompanied by chills, nausea, and vomiting. Fever does not have a fixed pattern like typhoid fever, often presenting as remittent. There are occasional cases of herpes labialis. Splenomegaly is relatively mild. Rose spots are smaller, atypical, and appear in large numbers. The Widal reaction in the urine is rarely positive. The course is short, about two or three weeks. Systemic symptoms are mild, and relapses or complications are rare.

Q: What are the symptoms of the gastroenteritis type?

A: Patients start with sudden vomiting and diarrhea; the symptoms are very severe, presenting as cholera or dysentery. Most food poisoning is this type. After eating spoiled meat, severe gastrointestinal symptoms suddenly occur within a few hours to ten hours, with fever, and herpes labialis is also seen.

Q: What phenomena do patients with cholera-like paratyphoid fever present?

A: Patients excrete rice-water-like stools in large quantities. They complain of thirst, hiccuping, and sudden loss of strength, loss of voice, and calf muscle cramps.

Q: What phenomena do patients with dysentery-like paratyphoid fever present?

A: Severe colic, stool mixed with mucus and blood, diarrhea, and tenesmus are seen.

Q: How long does the entire course of paratyphoid fever last? What is the outcome?

A: Regardless of the type of paratyphoid fever, it usually takes one week to three weeks to return to normal. Sometimes it lasts for five or six weeks or more, and the patient may fall into exhaustion.

Q: How should paratyphoid fever be accurately diagnosed?

A: Serum should be tested, or a bacteriological examination should be performed on the stool.

Q: How dangerous is this disease?

A: It's okay. But the gastroenteritis type is not good. The mortality rate is about 5%.

Q: What is the treatment method?

A: For the gastroenteritis type, castor oil should be given at the beginning, and at the same time, the stomach should be washed, activated charcoal should be taken internally, such as Atsu Gen, blood charcoal, etc., and then a mild laxative should be taken. The typhoid fever type can be treated like typhoid fever.

Q: How to prevent paratyphoid fever?

A: Inspect the slaughterhouses and avoid eating undercooked meat. In addition, refer to typhoid fever. (End)

Scientific Childbirth (27) 189

— Yu Songyun

Twenty-three: Diseases of the Breast

(A) Insufficient Breast Milk

Although there is breast milk after childbirth, it is not sufficient, sometimes it stops, or stops completely. This is due to the mother's lack of nutrition or mental stimulation. In addition, if there is excessive fat in primiparous women, or the mammary glands of multiparous women have atrophied because they did not breastfeed last time, these are all causes of insufficient breast milk.

Treatment for insufficient breast milk; in addition to ingesting more nutrients and all symptomatic treatments, artificial sun lamp irradiation can also promote the secretion of mammary glands. However, after a pregnant woman gives birth, she assumes the responsibility of breastfeeding her own child, so insufficient breast milk or complete stoppage after childbirth is unfortunate for the baby. Therefore, the mother should maintain her mind and body during pregnancy to be strong and disease-free, so that the breast milk can be pure and sufficient after childbirth, which is the fundamental solution.

(B) Excessive Breast Milk

The secretory function of the mammary glands is extremely vigorous. Breast milk still overflows after breastfeeding, gushing continuously, or it is thin as water, all of which are symptoms of excessive breast milk. Therefore, the mother is often prone to nutritional disorders, anemia, weakness, and other diseases.

If you have excessive breast milk, you should immediately eat less foods that produce milk, or use cloth bandages to tightly press the breasts, or use a breast pump to suck out the breast milk, all of which are possible. If the breasts feel painful, you can apply lard or Vaseline.

(C) Breast Milk Accumulation

If the secretion of the mammary glands is not excreted according to the amount, it will cause symptoms of accumulation, commonly known as breast heat. When breast heat occurs, the mammary glands are tense and feel painful as if they are being pressed. It mostly occurs on the third or fourth day of puerperium. At the same time, the body temperature is often above 38 degrees. You can use wet cloth bandages to press the breasts and take Glauber's salt. If the pain is severe, you can apply belladonna plaster.

(D) Mastitis

Pyogenic bacteria enter through the damaged part of the breast skin, and mastitis is formed. It mostly occurs within the second to sixth week of puerperium. At the beginning, there is high fever and chills, and the breast feels painful, often becoming a diffuse infiltration. If the fever persists, the affected area becomes red and swollen.

After suffering from mastitis, if it is not very serious, there is no need to rush to stop breastfeeding, because sometimes breastfeeding can cure it. However, you need to use a wet cloth ice pack to lift the nipple, or perform a warm compress, and then the tension can be reduced and suppuration can be prevented.

On the Importance of Physical Chemistry and Medicine 190

— Yu Gong

The level of physics and chemistry courses in our country's middle schools is uneven. Occasionally, a few schools have equipment that is barely satisfactory. However, there are really only a few instruments that can be used by students to do individual experiments, like phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. Therefore, the general knowledge of physics and chemistry of high school graduates is mostly insufficient. Therefore, they must continue to be taught after entering medical school.

Physics deduces the changes in force, and chemistry analyzes the content of matter. In the process of human life, there are extremely complex and subtle changes at all times. All changes are nothing more than force and matter. If you study medicine without starting from physics and chemistry, there is absolutely no possibility of solving it. In the past, a certain British authority on physiology once said that all physiological problems ultimately depend on chemistry and physics to be solved. This is an experienced statement.

According to the two subjects of chemistry and physics, the relationship is the main destiny, not only animals are like this, but plants are also not unique. For example, plants are sown in the ground. If they can suit the soil and climate, the food and nutrients contained in the seeds, such as proteins, hydrogen, oxygen, and sugars, are chemically transformed into roots, beards, stems, and trunks. The roots and beards absorb various minerals from the ground downwards, and the stems and trunks absorb carbon dioxide upwards, so as to flourish and grow. The chemical changes in between are endless. In the past, biologists used microscopes to explore the cells of animals and plants and their tissues, thinking they had succeeded. However, the cells contain countless atoms, and the cells themselves have functions such as breathing and secretion. Metabolism, the transformation and evolution in this, cannot be understood only by relying on microscopes. And the use of chemistry is even more important.

In terms of pharmacology, for example, Atropine can dilate the pupils and invalidate vision. After two or three days, but due to the progress of chemical research, Homatropine was invented. Its effect is equal to Atropine, but vision invalidates for only two or three hours. Another example is morphine, which is a holy drug for pain relief, and at the same time, it has the possibility of addiction. Through chemical research, Codeine was invented. Its effect can sometimes replace morphine without the drawbacks of addiction. Another example is caffeine, which is a diuretic, but its effect is often unreliable. After chemical research, Cocaine was discovered. Its chemical structure is similar to caffeine, but its diuretic effect is better. Later, theophylline was discovered. Its diuretic effect is even more pronounced than Cocaine. Another example is leprosy. Its specific drug is chaulmoogra oil. However, the oil is rich in irritants, which can cause patients to vomit. After chemical research, the components that stimulate vomiting were extracted. Its acidic substances are dissolved in alcohol and can be used for subcutaneous injection, which is a long-term treatment for leprosy. Another example is that the effective atom of quinine is in the CHOH class, and the effect of adrenaline on stimulating the sympathetic nerves is in the Catechol class. To fill the category to the end is countless. Therefore, if you do not know chemistry, but want to study medicine, it is like sailing on a disconnected and exhausted harbor and looking forward to reaching the sea.

Speaking of physics, its importance is equal to chemistry. The human body is like a machine. The wheels and gears are not wrong. In the process of life, cold and heat come and go, and the new replaces the old. The ingenuity of its function is even more amazing than machines. The swinging of the machine without conflict relies on the spring for buffering. The blood in the human body also has a spring for buffering. The so-called Buffer can keep the alkalinity in the blood from drastic changes. The human need for food is like the machine's need for fuel. In the machine, the rotation of the wheels, the discharge of steam, and the movement of the pistons all have rhythms that cannot be disturbed in the slightest. Imitating the human body, the contraction and expansion of the heart, the inhalation and exhalation of breathing, and the secretion of the skin, how can there be the slightest disorder. Therefore, to talk about medicine without learning the principles of physics is to abandon the root and pursue the branch. How can it be helpful?

The importance of chemistry and physics in relation to medicine is so important. Scholars in various countries around the world regard it as a basic science and stipulate that students must study it to a considerable extent before they can study medicine. However, their methods are extremely inconsistent. Britain, Germany, and other countries stipulate that students must continue to take remedial courses in basic science after entering medical school. In the United States, students do not need to take remedial courses after entering medical school after completing the basic science credits in college. Speaking of the German system, the graduates of Ober Realschule are more trained in chemistry, physics, and other subjects than those who graduated from Classical Gymnasunn by more than half. Both types of students must take remedial courses after entering medical school. However, those from Type A schools waste time reviewing old lessons. The American system is more reasonable, but the level and equipment of high schools are extremely uneven. Even in college, the credits taken are not very different in quantity, but the quality is still very uneven. It is not perfect. Although the unevenness of the world's school system has its advantages and disadvantages, the importance of basic science in relation to medicine is undeniable. Studying in school requires knowledge of physics and chemistry to understand. Even if you open a business and ask the world in the future, you will not be able to browse magazines and papers without a considerable level of physics and chemistry. Moreover, students have few opportunities to take remedial courses once they leave school. Therefore, they must have sufficient training before entering medical school.

Several Important Discoveries and Inventions in the Development of Modern Medicine (6) 191

— Gu Shoubai

Around 1870, the study of infectious diseases caused by trauma was at its peak. Mr. Klebs discovered spherical microbes in suppurative wounds during the Franco-Prussian War. However, some scholars at the time did not believe in the theory of microbes, thinking that infectious diseases of trauma were the result of putrefactive fermentation. It was not until 1876, when Koch discovered the developmental state of the anthrax bacillus, the process of spore formation, and the route of infection in animals, and subsequently discovered various microbes, that microbiology gradually developed.

As for the methods of culturing various microbes, since 1858, liquid culture media, potatoes, gelatin, solidified blood serum, broth, agar, and other culture media have been gradually applied, and various microbes can be cultured using these artificial methods. In terms of microscopic examination, Salomonssen, Koch, Ehrlich, and others used 'aniline' dyes to invent microbial staining methods. In 1884, Gram invented his special staining method. In 1890, Löffler invented a method for staining bacterial flagella.

Pasteur made many contributions to academia throughout his life, the most important of which are the following three:

The first discovery was the fact that [fermentation is caused by the presence of specific microorganisms]. In 1858, Pasteur followed up on his research on tartaric acid fermentation and published a paper on alcoholic fermentation. He discovered that sugar solutions were decomposed into alcohol and carbon dioxide due to the presence of microorganisms, and thus attributed fermentation to the action of microorganisms.

The second discovery was the fact that [infectious diseases are caused by the proliferation of specific microorganisms in the body]. At that time, the French silk industry was greatly affected by silkworm disease. In 1865, the government ordered Pasteur to focus on studying the cause of silkworm disease: after five years of painstaking effort, he discovered two pathogenic microbes and subsequently determined a method of prevention.

His discovery regarding fermentation further led people to think about the study of pathogens, which was a natural trend. At the time, he believed that since the fermentation of lactic acid, alcohol, butyric acid, etc., was caused by the action of microorganisms, then the cause of suppuration might also be due to microorganisms. Thus, he went from being a pure chemist to a biologist and medical scientist. Later, Davaine discovered the anthrax bacillus, Koch successfully purified and cultured the bacillus, and Pasteur repeatedly experimented with the bacillus, confirming it as the pathogenic bacterium of anthrax in 1877. In the same year, he discovered the malignant edema bacillus, which was the first discovery of an anaerobic pathogen. Subsequently, staphylococci and streptococci were discovered. After these pathogenic microbes were discovered one after another, Pasteur abandoned Liebig's chemical contact theory of disease and Virchow's pathogenic cell theory or parasitic cell theory, and confirmed the microbial theory.

The third discovery was the application of prophylactic vaccination. After Pasteur injected the virus of chicken cholera into the body of chickens and saw that they were no longer infected, he came up with the method of prophylactic vaccination. He implemented prophylactic vaccination for anthrax bacillus, reducing the mortality rate of sheep with anthrax from 25-30% to 1%, and the mortality rate of cattle to 0.34%. In addition, he discovered the fact that the virulence of pathogens can change after passing through animal bodies several times. The prophylactic vaccination for rabies is an application of this fact.

In 1867, Sir Joseph Lister, a surgeon in Glasgow, after learning about Pasteur's microbial theory of fermentation, applied antiseptic sterilization methods in surgical operations and achieved good results (see above). Therefore, the development of modern surgery and the glorious development and great progress in practical medicine such as the prevention of traumatic infectious diseases and puerperal fever are all greatly related to Pasteur's research. In this light, isn't Pasteur's contribution extremely great?

Many scholars emerged from Pasteur's school, publishing many extremely valuable achievements, such as Metchnikoff, who founded the phagocytic cell theory, Roux, who discovered diphtheria toxin, Yersin, who discovered the plague bacillus, Calmette, who implemented snake venom prophylactic vaccination, and Chamberland, who invented bacterial filters, all of whom were famous scholars.

Now, let's describe Koch's contributions to microbiology.

Koch's important work was to isolate pathogens, attempt pure culture, determine their pathogenicity, and discover many microbes. Since Koch, the development of microbiology has improved day by day, and the study of pathogens has since had a solid scientific basis; this is worthy of our attention and gratitude.

Comparing the differences between Pasteur and Koch in microbiological research, they are roughly as follows:

(1) Pasteur mainly used liquid culture media, discovered pathogens through original methods, separated and cultured them, or tested for changes in toxicity. Koch, however, used solid culture media.

(2) Pasteur mainly extracted pure pathogens from living animal bodies or corpses. Koch used the plate culture method to separate and purely culture the specific microbe he wanted to extract from the mixture of various microbes, avoiding the simultaneous occurrence of mixed bacteria.

(3) Pasteur often examined living pathogens under a microscope, while Koch used staining methods to make pathogens easier to see.

In 1882, when Pasteur discovered the pathogen of swine erysipelas and came up with the method of prophylactic vaccination using attenuated pathogens, Koch also discovered the tuberculosis bacillus. In 1884, when Pasteur enthusiastically studied the pathology and treatment of rabies, Koch also devoted all his efforts to studying the treatment and prevention methods of tuberculosis, the great enemy of mankind.

Before Koch, although someone had already discovered the rod-shaped bacterium of anthrax, it was not until 1876 that the pure culture and animal experiments of this pathogenic bacterium were completed by Koch. This was his initial contribution to microbiology. Subsequently, he successively invented the bacterial specimen fixation method, the [aniline] staining method, the photomicrography method, and the research on six pathogens of traumatic infectious diseases, and his reputation grew day by day. In 1881, he invented the pure culture medium; the following year, he discovered the tuberculosis bacillus and invented the dry heat sterilization method; in 1883, he traveled to India and Egypt for academic research and discovered the cholera vibrio and its transmission route; in 1890, he invented tuberculin; in 1892, when cholera was epidemic in Hamburg, he engaged in epidemic prevention work; in 1897, he invented a new tuberculin; in 1906, he studied African sleeping sickness and tried to treat it with [atoxyl]; and in 1905, he won the Nobel Prize.

Many famous scholars also emerged from Koch's school, such as Gaffky, Löffler, Pfeiffer, Welch, and Kitazato, all of whom made great contributions to microbiology and parasitology. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Sitting Bored 192

— Xiao Xue

Sitting here bored, I want to write something, but I don't know what to write.

I randomly opened a magazine, and the first thing I saw was a story about Emperor Yang of Sui. It said that Xue Daoheng wrote a good poem, "Swallows' mud falls from the empty beam," and Emperor Yang of Sui, ashamed of his inferiority, killed him and asked his corpse, "Can you still write 'Swallows' mud falls from the empty beam'?" I think this story is not bad, with the charm of Salome kissing John's head. But then I thought that high talent also leads to beheading, and I couldn't help but sigh: it's better not to write!

Because of Emperor Yang of Sui, I thought of Li Houzhu. He was captured and brought south, imprisoned in Jinling, and he was quite depressed, so he poured his feelings into poetry. One day, he was probably full of complaints again, and wrote the line "The old country is unbearable to look back on in the bright moon" in his poem. Who knew he would be killed because of this? Nostalgia is not allowed, and I can't help but feel something again, and sigh again: it's better not to write!

Association is a monster. From Li Houzhu, it jumped very far, and I thought of many literary inquisitions in the Qing Dynasty, such as "Lu Lijin's Snow Crime Travelogue," "Record of the Case of the Fang and Dai Families in Tongcheng," and even the far-fetched bloody cases of the "Gentle breeze does not know characters, why does it turn the pages of the book?" I feel that literary people are truly at the end of the road. Except for being dogs, they have no freedom. One careless stroke can lead to decapitation, and I can't help but feel sad and sigh three times: it's better not to write!

In fact, not writing doesn't guarantee that you won't be killed. I remember a few years ago in Anhui, someone was arrested for a bottle of red ink; in Hunan, someone was killed for reading Guo Moruo's "Fallen Leaves"; in Jiangwan, a student was detained for three weeks for having a Soviet novel. Writing is extremely dangerous, and reading behind closed doors can also lead to unexpected disasters. Where do the intellectual classes ultimately go? Here, I can't help but praise Hitler's sagacity and decisiveness. Like Qin Shihuang, burning books and burying scholars is a more thorough solution. The affair of beheading for writing, I don't know the gains and losses, I put the book aside, it's better not to write!

The poet Han Qibo from my hometown said: "Outside the window, the sky is like ink, a lamp shines sadly like a flower, wanting to talk about the future, my heart is already as chaotic as hemp." The poet's state of mind is truly sad. Although the heart is as chaotic as hemp, the road ahead must still be opened up. The road is full of thorns, and knives and guns are against our necks, but we still have to advance with blood. But "A scholar is worth nothing," it's better not to write!

Sitting here bored, I want to write something, what should I write?

"Translation" and "Compilation" 193

— Lin Yizhi

Mr. Ling Jing said the following on the "Free Talk" the other day about "compilation" and "writing": "People who are undertaking the task of cultural movement now, instead of focusing on translating foreign masterpieces, why not take the time to do some work of compilation and rewriting." Because of many hard-to-read hard translations, I agree with his view, and I have expressed the same opinion when the popular edition of "Destruction" came out. However, at the same time, I can't help but have some doubts:

If many people who are doing hard translations and random translations were to switch to doing "compilation and rewriting," would they be competent? We know that if you have a deeper understanding of a work when translating it, no matter how profound the work is, no matter how different the Chinese and foreign grammars and customs are, it will never be as stiff as many current translations are, making people afraid to understand. I heard that there are many translators now who don't even bother to read the original work from beginning to end. They open the first line and translate, and there is no way to talk about understanding the original work. I heard a joke that an old bookstore owner read the Chinese translation of Gorky for forty years and said that Gorky's articles were not well written. Therefore, "these books have no sales at all," and what is negotiable is not the translation work itself, but the attitude of translation.

However, because of the separation of habits, customs, etc., even very faithful translations often cannot be understood by those who lack preparatory knowledge. If someone can do the work of summary and popular compilation, such as the popular edition of "Destruction" and "The Iron Flood," it is also very important at the moment. But I think this compilation work is really much more difficult than translation. If you also use the attitude of hard translation and random translation to do it, the result will definitely be worse. Maybe "summary" will become "fragmentation," and "popularization" will become "vulgarization" or "distortion." Because here, in addition to a deep understanding of the original work, a comprehensive education is even more needed. For example, we already have many translations and summaries about "dialectical materialism," but it is difficult to find a popular small booklet on this theory compiled by ourselves. There is no other reason, because the person who can make a popular explanation of the most profound theories is the person who can have the most profound research on this theory. Obviously, we still lack scholars who can conduct thorough and painstaking research on a theory and apply it at will.

So, overall, the problem is not in translation or compilation, but in the attitude of scholars in researching academics!

About Lan Caihe 194

— Dian

The previous article "Lan Caihe is Not a Fairy" only cited Lu You's "Southern Tang Book" as evidence. Trivial matters are not worth arguing about, which is the first meaning. Moreover, the theory of immortals is absurd and difficult to verify, and whether Lan Caihe himself exists is still questionable, so how can we have time to distinguish whether he is male or female? The reason why I argue even when it is unnecessary to argue is that I compare myself to Zhuangzi, who thought the world was turbid and could not be discussed with Zhuangzi. I didn't expect that the madman's dream could not be said in front of him, and it actually brought out many wonderful theories from people like Hu Huaichen.

Zhao Yi's "Gaiyu Congkao" Volume 34, roughly says that there are two female immortals in the popular legend of the Eight Immortals, Lan Caihe and He Xiangu. It also says that Yuan Yishan has the sentence "I am surprised that Bai Yu is ahead of Pan Yue, and people laugh at the blue shirt like Caihe." His inscription on Lan Caihe's portrait says: "The long board sings without madness, and the children are busy for a hundred coins. When will I meet the old man in the blue shirt and dance with him in the spring breeze?" It is Lan Caihe is a man. Today's operas forcibly dress him as a woman, which is even more ridiculous." Zhao Yi has already investigated that Lan Caihe is not a female immortal, but the compilers of modern literary dictionaries do not know this. I pointed it out, but some people came forward to argue, and I don't know what to do.

Regarding Lan Caihe, Zhao Yi's "Gaiyu Congkao" has omissions, so I will add a few more details. "Shuofu" Volume 43, Tang Shen Fen's "Continued Biographies of Immortals," lists sixteen people who ascended to immortality, with a note saying "Three women inside." These three people are listed at the end, namely Xie Ziran, Pei Xuanjing, and Qi Xiaoyao. As for Lan Caihe, he is listed second among the sixteen people, saying that he is "unknown from where." Shen Fen, who lived in the remnants of the Tang and Five Dynasties, did not know who Lan Caihe was, but he had already affirmed that Lan Caihe was a male immortal, which is clearly evident. Also, upon investigation, the Yuan Dynasty miscellaneous drama included an anonymous "Han Zhongli Du Lan Caihe," in which Lan Caihe appeared and said: "My surname is Xu, my name is Jian, and my stage name is Lan Caihe. My whole family is fond of a thousand gold, and the son born is Xiao Caihe, and the daughter-in-law is Lan Shan Jing." From Shen Fen, Lu You, to Yuan Yishan and others, they all said that Lan Caihe was a male immortal, so it can be known that in the legends of the Five Dynasties, Song, and Yuan Dynasties, Lan Caihe was still not a female immortal. Zhao Yi said that it is popularly said that Lan Caihe is a female immortal, and that today's operas forcibly dress him as a woman. Then, the theory that Lan Caihe is a female immortal probably originated in the Ming and Qing Dynasties. Since He is planning to write about the Eight Immortals, will he have an answer as to whether Lan Caihe is male or female among the Eight Immortals? We can wait for it.

Pearl S. Buck, Author of "The Good Earth" (Continued) 195

— Yi Xian

After marrying Professor John Lossing Buck, Head of the Department of Agricultural Economics at Nanjing and Jinling University, she gave birth to a daughter who was very good-looking but suffered from a disability from birth. Ms. Buck had to send her to a specialized educational institution in the United States to spend her lonely life there. However, Ms. Buck was always concerned about the future of this poor daughter. "I have to raise enough money for this daughter's lifetime expenses before I can feel at ease! But Mr. Buck's teaching income is very limited, and I am penniless, so where will I get so much money? I think I should work hard to write and use the profits from writing to solve this problem."

These frank words were said by Ms. Buck to Mr. Long Moxiong, a strike friend, who helped her collect materials for the history of Chinese novels.

In the spring of 1927, the Nanjing Incident broke out, and Ms. Buck took refuge in Shanghai, living in a small Western-style house next to Shanzhong Road, where she devoted herself to writing. Her first published novel, "East Wind: West Wind," was completed that year.

In the spring of the following year, the situation stabilized, and Ms. Buck returned to Nanjing and continued to engage in long-form writing. She got up every morning, washed and dressed briefly, and went to a small room on the third floor to write at her desk, returning to the upstairs after breakfast until noon, when she stopped writing, and then did other things in the afternoon. Under these circumstances, "The Good Earth," which later caused a sensation in the European and American literary circles, was produced.

"East Wind: West Wind" describes the conflict between new and old ideas in a Chinese family in the form of a self-narrative by Guilan, a traditional Chinese woman. With its oriental atmosphere and beautiful writing, this novel received rave reviews from British and American newspapers after its publication. But the work that gave her a definite reputation in the American literary world and made her a fortune was "The Good Earth." "The Good Earth" was published in New York in March 1931 and was selected as a masterpiece by the New Book Selection Committee organized by the American publishing industry. Soon after, she won the 1931 Pulitzer Prize for Literature. Although the amount of this prize was only 5,000 US dollars, it was very reputable in the United States, and the glory was extraordinary. The structure of "The Good Earth" is based on the life of a farmer and woven with the disasters of droughts, floods, soldiers, and bandits. What the author has grasped are simply the most serious problems currently facing poor China. The protagonist, Wang Lung, can be regarded as the model of the peasants who make up the majority of China's population. The first half of his life represents the hunger and poverty of the peasants, while the second half represents the wealthy peasants with a comfortable life. The author broke away from the causal moral concept of "diligence and thrift leads to wealth," and instead used the riots of urban slum dwellers as the turning point in Wang Lung's life. This is where the author's greatness lies. Perhaps because she strived to cater to the tastes of the American public, the author portrayed Chinese ethics and etiquette too excessively, and her description of the sexual psychology of Chinese people who worship Lin Daiyu-style female beauty also seemed somewhat unnatural. Therefore, our country's readers are often not very satisfied with the second half of "The Good Earth." However, from a critical point of view, the success of "The Good Earth" is obviously not in those love scenes, but in the touching descriptions of the tragic famines. Such a novel depicting poverty finally made the author a rich person in a world of economic downturn. This was indeed beyond the author's expectations. The author now no longer needs to worry about her poor daughter's lifetime expenses, and like the situation when Wang Lung was about to leave the big city in the south, she suddenly got a lot of gold coins, enough for her to travel long distances in Europe and the United States and live a prosperous life in the future.

"The Good Earth" more or less changed Westerners' views of our country, and the actual impact is worth noting. In the autumn of 1931, just when "The Good Earth" was popular in the United States, our country suffered a serious flood. In the relief funds received by the government from abroad, donations from Americans accounted for the majority. According to the letter written to the author by the president of the American Red Cross, the reason was that the story of the Wang Lung family encountering drought deeply moved Americans.

Following "The Good Earth," "Sons" was published. This describes the lives of Wang Lung's three sons after his death. The three of them represent Chinese gentry, merchants, and warlords. However, the author obviously does not have the same sympathy and understanding for these types of Chinese people as she does for the peasants, and therefore it was not as successful as "The Good Earth." Ms. Buck returned to the United States with Mr. Buck in July 1930 and personally witnessed the popularity of her work there. She just left the United States in late June this year. Now she is probably traveling in Europe. In the near future, we will be able to see this happy female writer who considers China her "second motherland." This time when she comes to China again, she will definitely be able to recognize this old, big, and poor China more deeply, so her future works may retain the advantages of "The Good Earth" and eliminate the shortcomings. While welcoming this kind author with enthusiasm, we can't help but hold this hope.

Ordinary Things (28) 196

— Yun Guo Sun

"That's a good idea!" Zhi Guang couldn't help but jump up with joy.

"Then shouldn't we complete the formalities now so that we can go to Zhabei tomorrow..."

Before Bo Tang could finish his words, the door of the study suddenly opened, and Pei Huang, carrying a hot water bottle that was more than a foot long and wearing a pair of leather rabbit shoes, walked into the room unhurriedly. She heard Bo Tang's unfinished sentence and asked...

"Going to Zhabei again?"

"That's right," Bo Tang said.

"Is your conversation over?"

"Not yet... but there is already a way to end it."

"How to end it?"

"Go to Zhabei! That's how to end it."

"Didn't Zhi Guang already go? Who is going now?"

"I am."

"When are you going?"

"Tomorrow morning."

"Nonsense... Zhi Guang ran away, which has already worried people a lot. It's hard to come back safely and peacefully, and now you say you want to go again, you must have eaten too much... This is really nonsense! You should listen to the sound of the cannons outside today. It's never been this loud!" Everyone listened carefully, but they didn't hear anything. Then Lian Pei Huang became suspicious. Finally, Bo Tang said with a smile...

"It's another castle in the air!"

"A castle in the air! You didn't hear it. Just now, when I was talking to them on the third floor, I really heard it very clearly. That kind of bi bi ba ba sound like boiling porridge, I don't care about it. What makes people annoyed the most is the peng peng peng one after another cannon sounds. It's never been this loud..."

Economic Weekly, Issue 33, Published Every Monday

Alas!! The Economic Policies of Various Nations by Pan Haoshi 197

(I) The London Conference Has Failed Again

In June 1932, the Lausanne Conference attempted to revive the world economy. On July 9, five agreements were established. The achievements were minimal, but hope remained in the fifth item, which called for the League of Nations to convene another world economic conference. In June of this year, this large-scale world economic conference was held in London, gathering elites from sixty-six nations, spending thirty-eight days of time. Capitalist gold standard kingdoms, socialist red internationals, and even those who were usually not considered for world conferences were invited to participate, forging together in one furnace, a grand and prosperous gathering. It was expected to resolve disagreements and cure incurable diseases. However, due to presumptuous self-confidence and infighting, the conference was fraught with difficulties. Consequently, it was adjourned on the 27th of this month. The outcome? Needless to say. Reopening the conference is a futile dream. Now, let's examine the important issues of this London Conference and briefly discuss its failure, which I believe is also of concern to the readers.

(I) Tariffs. Tariff wars have always been a common term in economic history. However, the breadth and depth of these wars have never been as severe as in recent years. The construction of tariff barriers is almost universal. (China, with its incomplete tariff autonomy, cannot be considered in the same light.) It is said that the current tariff war tactics employed by various countries range from common strategies such as prohibiting imports, limiting imports, increasing tariffs, encouraging exports, and reciprocal treatment, to special strategies such as state-run trade and state-run exchange. If broken down, there could be more than two hundred types. This is no exaggeration. Every country seeks to increase its exports while reducing its imports. The international trade arena is filled with countless barriers. The international trade index has been decreasing year by year, with the Soviet Union being the only exception. As a result, countries are greatly concerned about the problem of falling prices and the increasing number of unemployed. Commentators attribute the economic panic to tariff wars. However, no country is willing to dismantle its barriers first, and every country hopes that others will dismantle theirs first. Therefore, the London Conference focused on this issue. When the United States proposed a 10% reduction in tariffs, there was an uproar. The Japanese Empire, which considers itself the "Germany of the East," was particularly opposed. The countries that advocated for the removal of tariff barriers were generally doing so for others. What they hoped for from other countries was merely a 10% reduction, while for their own countries, they would maintain their existing barriers as the lowest line of defense. As a result, the tariff issue had to be withdrawn. Commentators said that the United States proposed tariff reductions because it had already gained a new weapon (devaluation of the gold standard), and no longer needed to maintain full tariff barriers to prevent imports. The opposition of France, Japan, and many other countries to a general reduction was because the United States was using the sharp decline in the gold standard exchange rate to vigorously develop exports, and tariffs were necessary to counteract this. Therefore, France often said that tariff discussions should take place after the exchange rate problem is resolved. Since the United States was unwilling to participate in a stable exchange rate policy, France, Japan, and other countries were also unwilling to lower their tariffs. Each country prioritized its own interests, making a resolution hopeless.

(II) Exchange Rates. The deviation of exchange rates from the norm has been long-standing. Since countries began to prohibit the export of gold, the disorder has worsened. Exchange rate policies are often subject to unpredictable changes, which constrain international investment and trade, and disrupt the international economic chain. Commentators often dream of the prosperity before the war, believing that the instability of exchange rates hinders the recovery of the world economy. However, after countries such as the United Kingdom and Japan prohibited the export of gold and devalued their foreign exchange rates, the international market prices of their commodities fell significantly, which helped their foreign trade. Therefore, regarding exchange rate psychology, they only hope that other countries will adjust, but are unwilling to raise their own rates, which is the same as the tariff issue. Since the recent economic panic in the United States, the gold standard was suspended, the currency was inflated, and the exchange rate of the gold dollar fell sharply. The international market price of American goods suddenly plummeted. Its exports were like a fierce tiger unleashed, invincible. Countries realized that their own exchange rate policies were insufficient to compete with the United States, so they proposed stabilization policies at the London Conference, with France as its leader. However, the United States regarded this as a weapon and was unwilling to give it up. As a result, the so-called international central bank system, international exchange rate fund system, and exchange rate agreements all became empty talk. The exchange rate problem ultimately vanished. The silver problem is a subset of the exchange rate problem and was also an important issue at the London Conference. Today, countries that use silver, such as China, India, and many other weak countries, are rich in silver reserves. The total population and total consumption power are astonishing. However, due to the drastic fall in silver prices, purchasing power has inevitably decreased. Countries that use gold, frustrated with the tariff and exchange rate issues, retreated to the silver problem, seeking a way out. The consensus was that if silver prices rose, it would develop the export trade of countries that use silver, and the cause of the world economic panic could be somewhat resolved. Thus, the Silver Subcommittee was established, and the Eight-Nation Agreement gradually emerged. Weak countries that use silver were fortunate that major gold-using countries were condescending and offering assistance, but they did not realize that they were opening up export markets for gold-using countries. How sad.

(III) War Debts. War debts have dominated the world economy for more than a decade. The United States is a creditor nation, Germany is a debtor nation, and the United Kingdom is a debtor to the United States and a creditor to other countries. France, Italy, and Belgium are creditors to Germany but debtors to the United States and the United Kingdom. As a result of offsetting debts and credits, Germany is undoubtedly a debtor, and France and Italy are also purely debtor nations. The United Kingdom is an intermediary country for debts and credits. Only the United States holds enormous credits, long dominating the world economy. European countries almost all rely on its decisions. Since the world economic panic of 1929, the finances of various countries have deteriorated daily. The issue of war debts has gradually become a problem that can be re-examined. However, the United States is using this to dominate the world and has not allowed the reduction of credits. After the expiration of Hoover's one-year moratorium plan in 1931, the United States repeatedly demanded repayment, while European debtor countries were reluctant. The London Conference first mentioned war [debts]. This was [omitted characters] and ultimately could not forget about revising [omitted characters]. The United States firmly opposed, and the war debt issue at the London Conference was like a fleeting glimpse.

The above issues encompass the important agendas of the London Conference, and it can be said that almost nothing was achieved. In addition, agreements such as the Wheat Agreement had minimal impact, and the resolution to curb investment was mere formality. Limiting production was even more empty talk. The failure of the conference is beyond doubt. The key to its failure was that each country sought to benefit itself at the expense of others, ultimately leading to mutual contradictions and achieving nothing.

(II) Economic Warfare or Military Warfare? 198

The convocation of world economic conferences is not a one-time event. The 1927 Geneva Conference was attended by fifty countries. At that time, although there were relatively concrete resolutions on tariff issues, after the meeting, tariff wars intensified. Subsequently, the Danube Conference and the Lausanne Conference had fewer participating countries, and the results were also very superficial. In recent months, with the United States suspending the gold standard, the world economy has become more depressed. The inability of the London Conference to fully meet expectations is not surprising. However, before the conference, countries had some expectations. They were restraining their policies, waiting for a change in the atmosphere during the conference. Now that the conference has ended in failure, most countries, either seeing the unwillingness of other countries to compromise or feeling their own backwardness, will abandon their illusions of international coordination and seek their own ways to revive. Then, the hideous face of capitalism will inevitably be increasingly exposed, and the following three paths will be inevitable:

(I) The Rise of Controlled Economy. Since the success of the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, although the world has felt the economic panic, it has been able to develop production and increase exports. Therefore, capitalist countries that oppose communism have also begun to advocate for economic control. They believe that the past development of capitalism focused on the rationalization of production, but there was no comprehensive plan for the national economy. As a result, the more rationalized each production enterprise became, the more irrational the national economy became. Therefore, it is necessary to reorganize the national front and seek economic control. From production enterprises to national trade and finance, everything should be subject to government control. This policy is essentially state capitalism. European and American countries have already adopted parts of it, such as exchange rate management. Now that the London Conference has failed, the international situation has become more tense. The scope of national control may expand.

(II) The Resumption of Trade and Financial Warfare. Tariff wars, exchange rate wars, dumping policies, and gold seizure policies in recent years are all related to trade and financial warfare. Tariffs are the center of trade warfare, and exchange rates are the center of financial warfare. Therefore, the London Conference addressed these issues first. Now that the conference has failed, the trend of international confrontation is becoming more apparent. World trade and finance have clearly lost their chain. Countries almost all feel the need to address overproduction and low prices, and strive for a trade surplus. In finance, they all seek to accumulate gold reserves to improve their national credit system. The continuation of tariff and exchange rate wars is inevitable. The overall trade and financial relations between countries may inevitably enter a state of war. In an era of rising economic control ideology, this kind of warfare is most likely.

(III) The Struggle for Markets. In recent years, countries have suffered not from a lack of production, but from the narrowness of sales channels. The most important goal of the London Conference was to remove obstacles to international trade and promote trade activities. Unfortunately, due to the unwillingness of countries to compromise, various obstacles have not been reduced. Moreover, since the outcome of the conference was poor, new obstacles will arise in the future. In disappointment, countries will inevitably engage in the struggle for markets to seek new economic colonies, or exclude the competition of other countries to seek exclusive control of existing markets. In the era of economic control and trade financial warfare, this kind of struggle is inevitable. The result may lead to military warfare. The fuse for the Second World War will be planted here.

The above three items can be summarized into two backgrounds. (I) The development of state capitalism... All national economic control, external aggression in trade and finance, and the struggle for economic colonies are characteristics of state capitalism. What the Soviet Union has done in recent years is no different. Although it claims to be communist domestically, it is a state capitalist country in the world economic arena. Because the state capitalism of various countries is not yet complete, the Soviet Union can gain an advantage in the world economic battlefield. Today, although countries avoid mentioning communism, they are all progressing in this direction. In the subsequent development process, the countries with the most developed statism will have the advantage, and there is a possibility of local prosperity in the world economy. However, as time passes, the international economy will be filled with these countries, and they will feel the lack of room for development. Although the economy of each country is rationalized (?), the economy of the whole world will inevitably feel irrational one day. Then the economic panic will inevitably overflow and become uncontrollable. Economists often say that although capitalism develops, it will inevitably self-destruct one day. This is the common conclusion obtained from academic research. (II) The formation of the International Confrontation Front... The situation of international confrontation will intensify due to the lack of coordination at the London Conference. Those with the same interests will inevitably unite to confront their common enemy. Europe already has this situation. The transformation of the international confrontation front from fragmented to integrated, from thin to thick, is undoubtedly inevitable. Reciprocal trade and financial alliances are inevitable trends. Moreover, the war debt problem has been a dispute for many years. The attitude of the United States at this conference has been watched by European countries, but there is nothing they can do. In the future, due to the struggle for economic hegemony and the distinction of war debt interests, the major opposing fronts in the international economy will become more prominent. The result will inevitably lead to military warfare, which cannot be ignored.

In short, in the future, countries will inevitably fall into the war of state capitalism without realizing it. Even the Soviet Union, which claims to be communist, cannot escape this. Although countries will strive to improve their domestic economic policies, the direction they are heading is wrong, and the fall is only a matter of time. In the meantime, many natural resources will inevitably be wasted and many human lives will be hindered. Westerners often [believe in] the creator, and there is God; then God is foolish.

(III) Not Worried About Poverty But Worried About Inequality 199

By exploring the economic policies of various countries before and after the London World Economic Conference, we not only feel their hideousness and fear, but also pity their ignorance and foolishness. I, a humble scholar, believe that there is still a way to change course. Please allow me to elaborate:

People often talk about economic panic, thinking that the situation is precarious and unsustainable. But let us try to examine whether the supply of materials is sufficient to meet the needs of human life. According to world statistics, the increase rate of population and materials in the world from 1925 to 1931 is as follows:

Population 5% Raw materials 25%

Food 10%

It can be seen that human life is not likely to experience poverty, so what is there to panic about? This is what is known as "those who produce are many, and those who consume are few." Since Malthus's theory of population was introduced, people have feared that the population would increase geometrically, while materials would only increase arithmetically. After witnessing the productivity of the industrial revolution, they realized that it was a needless worry. Today, the increase in goods is clearly greater than the population. However, countries are loudly complaining about the economic panic, the large number of unemployed, and poverty. At the same time, they are recording the increasing rate of inventories, the declining prices, and the artificial methods of suppressing production. Is this not strange? Materials are not insufficient, but the majority of the population feels insufficient consumption, and the unemployed have nothing to live on. Capitalists who accumulate inventories often complain about the excessive productive capacity and the insufficient turnover of funds. They even destroy some of their goods to prevent price declines. As a result, there are those who cause price declines due to sluggish sales and delay repayment of debts. There are those who affect the financial world due to the collapse of credit. There are those who cause tariff problems due to the promotion of foreign exports and the restriction of imports. There are those who cause exchange rate problems due to the instability of trade and finance. There is unemployment due to limited production or business failure. There are [omitted characters] due to the decline of the economy, and there are financial defects. There are those who cause currency inflation due to financial defects, or unstable markets and finance. There are also those who, due to currency inflation, lead to disputes over international exchange finance and trade. The root cause of the recent new world economic panic is nothing more than this. The root cause is purely unequal distribution. Only with unequal distribution do capitalists focus only on surplus value, so there is so-called overproduction. Only with unequal distribution do workers and the general middle and lower classes have no surplus purchasing power, so there is so-called material surplus. The Great Learning says, "Not worried about poverty but worried about inequality." The pathology of the world economy can be viewed in this way. Since the disease lies in "inequality," it should be treated with "equality." Therefore, if we want to save the world economy from disaster, we should have the production and distribution of the economy managed by society. Make everyone do their best and make the best use of their goods. Rivalry and contention have no way to profit. And the hideous face of capitalism will disappear by itself. I, a humble scholar, believe that countries should realize this and move in this direction.

Furthermore, the financial defects of various countries are also a factor contributing to economic panic. Currency inflation is inevitable. Even the raising of tariffs is sometimes due to fiscal reasons. The root cause of financial defects is militarism. War debts are only a small part of it. According to a survey by the League of Nations, 70% of the budgets of European Christian countries are spent on past and future expenses. The British Chancellor of the Exchequer also said in 1930 that global military spending reached 900 million gold pounds annually. The direct harm of militarism to the economy is already like this. The indirect harm must be even more alarming. Therefore, I believe that countries should immediately change their policies, and even the smallest effect can prevent the economy from becoming bleak again. However, at a time when countries are selfishly using their own interests, they are using military force as a backing for their economic warfare, so this level is difficult to achieve before policies are changed. Therefore, to get to the root of the problem, we should still focus on the economic reforms mentioned above. Japan is too busy seeking expansion, so there is no possibility of reducing [military spending]. This is why the disarmament conference has not achieved anything, and the world disaster is difficult to eliminate.

The Main Reason for the Failure of the Economic Conference by Chu 200

Since the opening of the London World Economic Conference on June 12, it has been more than a month, and it is difficult to achieve the expected results. This has been known for some time. Now, the economic conference has ended in failure. There are many reasons for its failure, and the biggest reason is that the purpose of the conference was not a purely economic issue, but was mixed with political functions. At the beginning of the conference, British Prime Minister MacDonald pretended to raise the issue of war debts in the political aspect. Although this issue was not on the agenda, France soon raised the issue of European political stability, which was more important to the conference; and President Roosevelt raised the issue of non-aggression treaties; The German representatives proposed the recovery of the old German colonial territories, etc., which suddenly changed the situation of the conference. Using the Quadripartite Agreement of England, Germany, France, and Italy as a wedge, the countries that stabilized the European political situation and sought to revise the peace treaties, such as Germany and Italy, were in opposition to the opinions of France, Poland, and the Little Entente countries. The responsibility country using the Quadripartite Agreement as a wedge was originally in the Little Entente countries. Czechoslovak Foreign Minister Benes was the most opposed to the Quadripartite Agreement. This is because Germany advertises absolute nationalism and wants to restore national power with strength. On the one hand, it rejects Jews, and on the other hand, it implements political party isolation, which are all manifestations of pursuing far-reaching goals. In this unstable situation, the success of an economic conference that takes the stability of the European political situation as a premise is possible? The failure of the disarmament conference is the cause of the European political unrest. The failure of the disarmament conference is a major obstacle to the economic conference. As a result, all countries have formed economic alliances based on their own interests in order to consolidate themselves. Such as the union of the United Kingdom with Canada, Australia, India, South Africa, Rhodesia, and other autonomous colonial territories; France's union with French Indochina, Algeria, and with Poland, Czechoslovakia, Romania, Yugoslavia, and other colonies with close ties; the United States' union with Argentina, Brazil, Colombia, and other South American countries; The union of Germany with Italy, Austria, and Hungary. Such opposing unions and alliances all adopt exclusive policies with economic nationalism. The two major propositions of the United States' currency inflation! Raising prices, and France's stable currency, to control production, are the major reasons for the failure of this conference. Therefore, if we truly want to save the world economy from its predicament, we must first abolish this kind of union control. Otherwise, all [countries] will go to extremes, despise international coordination, and be eager for economic nationalism, then the future of the world economy will be even more unimaginable. After economic integration, countries will inevitably set up preferential tariffs, or agree on reciprocal tariffs, or raise tariffs on third countries, and devote themselves to market competition. As a result, the world's finances will inevitably fall into a state of chaos, and the industrial economy of various countries will gradually decline.

A Glimpse of Peiping's Social Economy (Continued) by Cheng Wen-ai 201

(1) Discount interest is divided into two types: cash (i.e., silver dollars) and transfer (i.e., checks). A handling fee of five cents per thousand yuan is charged.

(2) Remittances are divided into Tianjin and Shanghai. A handling fee of five cents per thousand yuan is also charged.

(3) Currency is divided into three types: Shanghai banknotes, Shanxi banknotes, and other banknotes. A handling fee of five cents per thousand yuan is charged. In addition, Peiping City has a stock exchange, established in 1918, with a capital of 600,000 yuan. Besides trading public bonds and treasury bills, only Qixin shares are listed. The years 1924, 1925, and 1926 were the most prosperous, with spot transactions being the most common. Transactions were relative, not competitive. Trading hours were after 12:00 noon daily. The exchange assumes full supervisory responsibility for both buyers and sellers. If one party breaches the contract, the exchange can compensate the other party for the losses suffered, and the exchange then recovers all losses from the breaching party. For stock transactions, a cash deposit of 400 yuan is required for every 10,000 yuan. The handling fee is five jiao per 5,000-yuan face value, collected from both buyers and sellers. The quota for brokers is 60, with each broker required to have a cash deposit of 5,000 yuan and be introduced by at least two members of the Brokers Association. After passing the examination, they are submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval before being recognized. Most of these brokers are silver firms, also operating this business. Currently, there are only a little over ten brokers remaining at the exchange, likely due to the decline of the market. As for Peiping's local financial issue, it is the copper coin problem. In recent years, because there have been many foreign copper coins, mostly from Tianjin, the authorities have banned them. If copper coins flood the market, small business owners and laborers will be the first to suffer, which would greatly affect society. As for the abolition of taels and the conversion to yuan, it has already been implemented de facto in Peiping. Currently, all transactions are without the tael unit, perhaps because Peiping does not have foreign exchange constraints!

5. Public Utilities and Labor-Management Issues Peiping's tram company is a joint venture between the government and merchants. The government shares are funded by the Sino-French Bank. There are not many tram lines in the city, and the tramcars are old. However, the passengers are very crowded, so its operating income is likely good. The tram uses a siren to signal departure, which is the same as the siren used in the city for emergencies. I think this is inappropriate. Electricity and tap water are entirely commercial, with the government only in a supervisory position. What is the scale and equipment of these public utilities? Because I have not visited them, I cannot speculate or criticize. However, according to a survey of tap water users in Peiping, the water supplied by the tap water company is very unclean, with a lot of yellow mud in the water. It must first be stored in a tank and allowed to settle before it can be used. This is also an area that public utilities should improve. As for Peiping, because there is a lack of large public factories, labor-management issues rarely occur. The only organized unions are the Tram Workers' Union and the Postal Workers' Union. When disputes occasionally arise, they can usually be resolved peacefully. It can be said that there have been no real labor strikes in Peiping in recent years.

6. Overview of the Standard of Living | | Conclusion

Due to the relocation of the capital, the general standard of living in Peiping has dropped a lot. Just take rent as an example. In the past, because it was the political center, there were many people chasing officialdom, so the demand for housing exceeded the supply, and rents could be increased as much as possible. However, after the political center moved south, the officials moved with it, so the supply of housing suddenly exceeded the demand, and rents fell by an unknown amount. Housing is no longer valuable, and land prices have also fallen. The fall in land prices has further reduced rents. Currently, the rent for a room in Peiping is no more than one yuan per month, and there are still concerns about not having customers. Since the September 18th Incident, residents of the Northeast have flocked to Peiping to seek refuge, which has increased the population of Peiping a lot. In other words, the need for housing has also increased a lot. However, speaking of this, there is an interesting thing worth mentioning: the general landlords in Peiping do not welcome Northeastern residents very much, because once they rent a place to live, they will never pay rent again, and the landlords are helpless. Although, there is something to discuss about this, because the general Northeastern residents have lost their real estate and farmland, and are displaced disaster victims. How should they be relieved? However, there must be concrete measures for government relief, otherwise, allowing them to disrupt the local social order is the fault of the authorities. In addition, the living conditions of rickshaw pullers can be used as an example. First, take Shanghai as an example. These people walk quickly, sweating profusely. Due to the high cost of living, they work all day, and may not even be able to eat their fill. Peiping is different. The deep impression we have of these rickshaw pullers is that they are neatly dressed and their rickshaws are beautiful. Some of their rickshaws are self-provided, and some are rented from others. The rent is at most twenty or thirty cents a day, and a small amount only requires fifty or sixty copper coins, so they can live comfortably as long as they earn five or six jiao a day. As mentioned above, the wages of workers in Peiping are generally only five or six yuan per month, which is very different from Shanghai. Finally, in a summary, it is a great pity that our country has so much cheap labor and does not use it to develop our country's industry! (End)

Public Bonds Able to Pass Stably 203

The bond market of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange last week was quite stable. It was observed that there was still a peaceful path, and the lost land in Luandong was gradually being recovered. Moreover, since the July futures had been settled on Friday for delivery, trading restrictions were until Tuesday, so the market had a phenomenon of squeezing shorts and longs at the beginning of the week, but there were no drastic rises or falls. Major changes often occur around delivery, but this time it was calm.

Based on the high price level, there should be more longs. Based on the trend of people's hearts, shorts will be squeezed. However, large short positions were prepared early. Most of the floating shorts from the previous week had been closed or rolled over, so this squeeze was relatively peaceful. Only on Monday, as there was still hope for a peaceful solution in the inspection situation, longs and shorts rose at the same time, and the market price rose by one and a half yuan. Tuesday was the last day of the July futures, but most of the floating longs and shorts had been squeezed flat, and it was also stable, with a relatively continuous rise of about half a yuan. On Wednesday, only the August futures were traded for one month, the market atmosphere was slack, and transactions were quite light, with the market price fluctuating slightly by seven or eight jiao. On Thursday, the September futures were added, and most of them were opened in sequence on the first day, with various gangs having slight needs, and the market price rebounded by six or seven jiao. On Friday, the July futures delivery was processed and the market was closed. On Saturday, due to slight selling by large accounts, the market gave back a few jiao. The overall trend of the week was between possible rises and falls, slightly higher than the previous week by several jiao to more than one yuan. Compared with the highest price on July 19, the difference was only about one yuan. If the current situation does not change, it should not be a revolving situation. The total transaction volume was 44,326,800 yuan, of which 26,800 yuan were spot transactions, and the total of futures salt tax and military occupation was 15,090,000, 5,190,000, the total of 19 customs duties was 5,450,000, the total of 20 coupon 20 customs duties was 7,260,000, the total of 96 positive six was 7,170,000, and the rest ranged from tens of thousands to hundreds of thousands.

Talks

Talking about Dogs 208

—Lie Huo

Generally speaking, dogs are one of the most loyal animals; that is, loyal to the masters who raise them. At the same time, because loyalty has certain inevitable benefits, dogs are generally loved by people and kept as pets. However, the Chinese have never valued dogs very much. Therefore, although the national crisis is so serious, there are various national salvation movements, but none has appeared concerning dogs alone. Only the "dog racing" business is said to be very good.

Even the treatment of dogs is very meager. The only food for dogs in the countryside is people's excrement. Sometimes they can't even eat urine, because excrement is not as cheap in the countryside as it is in the city, but a unique fertilizer for farming. Therefore, if dogs want to eat, they can only steal, stealing by prying doors and climbing tanks. If they steal from their own masters, it doesn't matter much, but if they steal from other people, there is a risk of being beaten. As for feeding rice, feeding good food, and having a comfortable life, that is a blessing that Chinese dogs never have.

Growing up in the city is not much better, except that they generally don't want to eat excrement.

So Chinese national dogs are just dogs, or else it is strange.

If we talk about foreign dogs, then there is a lot to say. There are many names, such as police dogs, pugs, and Pekingese, and there are even special names for them. In short, there are all kinds. And the things they eat are even more exquisite. It is said that some dogs specialize in eating beef, while others prefer milk or buttered bread. Not only do they eat well, but they also have other preferential treatment, which is simply better than people. For example, foreign dogs don't like to walk, and want to ride in cars like people. When it's cold, they are also afraid of the cold, so they need to warm themselves by the stove and wear clothes. These things are annoying to people. Especially young foreign women who like to lead a male dog are not taken seriously by the Chinese. Therefore, Beijing once issued an order prohibiting women from learning from foreign women to lead male dogs on the street, saying that it was related to morals.

However, the loyalty of dogs does not have any boundaries. Chinese dogs and foreign dogs are all the same.

When I was a child, I read many articles about "righteous dogs." The word "righteous" is the ultimate loyalty. The fact is generally like this: "A certain person raised a dog, and one day took it to a certain place. On the way, they suddenly encountered a wild beast. The beast pounced on the person, and the dog protected him, so he was saved from danger." The author then used this to educate people and warn the world, always ending like this: "Alas, can a person be inferior to a dog!" or "Alas, even a beast is like this, how can a person be!" This kind of dog is a model of dog loyalty, and can simply be a teacher for people. From this, we can see that the Chinese value dogs because they value their loyalty so much. Later, when I taught elementary school, the first lesson in the Chinese textbook I used was: "Dog, big dog, little dog, big dog barks, little dog jumps, bark once, jump once, brother pretends to be a dog..." Dog brother and dog brother, going on and on with dogs. At that time, I was very strange. Teaching children with this kind of knowledge would inevitably make them learn to be a wagging dog. Later, I dropped out of teaching and came to Shanghai to study, and I gained a deeper understanding of the meaning of dog. Reading books and newspapers, I often saw the name "running dog," which meant that someone was enslaved and raised by someone, like a dog raised by someone. Once, there was a riot in the school, and the words on the wall newspaper were all "dog fights." This faction scolded that faction's people as so-and-so's running dogs, and that faction scolded this faction's people as whose righteous dogs. At this point, it was completely proven that in this world, there are indeed running dogs.

When I entered the door of society, the terms "running dog" and "comrade pug" were heard and seen everywhere.

Now it is truly a world of dogs. People who can "run" and can "dog" probably have some way to survive, otherwise it would be difficult to ensure that their stomachs don't panic.

However, there are also exceptions to the loyalty of dogs, such as "mad dogs" and "rabid dogs," which simply don't recognize their masters. There must also be this kind among "running dogs," but they are ultimately exceptions and a minority.

Congratulations 'Get Rich'! 209

— Bin Fu

Haha! Gentlemen, Ladies, Young Masters, Young Ladies!

It's finally here! Haha, today is; 'July 31st'!

Haha! Gentlemen, Ladies, Young Masters, Young Ladies!

The 'July 30th' calendar page has already been torn off, today, without a doubt, is 'July 31st'!

Haha! Gentlemen, Ladies, Young Masters, Young Ladies! It's 'July 31st,' time to 'Get Rich'! Haha!
