Gentlemen, Ladies, Young Masters, Young Ladies, I further tell you, today is just the preview of 'Getting Rich'. The 'shining silver dollars' or the 'fragrant checks' will have to wait until the seventh of next month!

Gentlemen, Ladies, Young Masters, Young Ladies, so I have to ask you, have you read the Three Principles of the People? If not, let me tell you, there's an interesting story in the first lecture of the Three Principles of the People, which is about a porter who bought a 'Get Rich Ticket.' He placed the lottery ticket in the middle of his carrying pole.

Later, he actually won the jackpot. He was so amused that he didn't want the carrying pole anymore and threw it into the river. By doing so, he lost his chance to 'Get Rich.' So even if you 'win the lottery' today, please don't throw away the 'Get Rich Ticket,' otherwise, you will be like 'that person' in the Three Principles of the People and 'lose everything'!

Modern Celebrities' Calligraphy and Painting No. 25 210

Calligraphy by Mr. Shen Siqi (Brief Biography)

Shen Weixian, zi Siqi, late sobriquet Tongweng, was from Huating, Jiangsu. He was a former Qing dynasty Xiaolian (recommended scholar) who served as a renowned county magistrate. When people from Songjiang served as officials, both Mr. Yang Guyun of Lou County and Mr. Shen Siqi of Huating were known as virtuous officials and were skilled in calligraphy and painting. In 1923, he served as the Speaker of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly. After resigning, he retired to the countryside, not concerning himself with worldly affairs, farming, raising silkworms, and devoting himself to calligraphy. Mr. Shen formerly specialized in the Six Dynasties style of calligraphy, but recently has been studying cursive script. As for his brushwork, it is elegant, vigorous, and his artistic spirit is profound, which is consistently his style.

A Blue Sky in Summer 211

— Yi Ping

Under the seductive gaze of neon lights, a group of young people entered, and the waiters in white were already bending at the waist, full of smiles, to welcome them. After rushing into the small dining room, the electric fans whirred madly, and everyone kept shouting how hot it was. The waiters, understanding, brought up several bottles of soda, which were snatched up eagerly. At this time, the entire room was noisy and chaotic. The young people were not willing to let go of any opportunity to make a commotion, and a dinner party was certainly a good Chance.

Eight people sat around a table, and after the waiters brought up the vegetarian dishes, they did not hypocritically shout "Please." Eighteen chopsticks were already simultaneously mobilized, turning the entire fish and meat into their captives. Those who were a little slow to act were often ridiculed by those who had grabbed the biggest piece on their chopsticks, and the person next to them would definitely bump into their shoulder, causing their captured item to fall onto the table, providing another round of grabbing for everyone. Therefore, the organization of their dinner party, the building of relationships, and the discussion of knowledge, etc., were all external propaganda. In reality, they were simply seizing a Chance to make a ruckus.

The weather was so hot that going to sit in the office every day was truly a torture, but no one was absent from the dinner party. The older chairman had proposed stopping it once last time, but was opposed by more than six members. As for the chairman, he was only slightly older in age, not truly old, and he could certainly participate in the fun and commotion as much as possible.

There were only a few so-called main dishes left on the table, and everyone's stomach seemed to need a break. So, new tricks were introduced at this time, and ordering songs from the hall was a program that had to be carried out every time at the dinner party. After everyone knowingly agreed, the temporary secretary began to write straight away. He would not misremember who was ordering Linglong and who was ordering Yueying. After the waiters sent out the slips, the group temporarily dispersed, two in a group, three in a pile, discussing sound movies, women's stories, or even more obscene tricks. The dinner party was indeed a good gathering for young people.

A sound of high-heeled leather shoes came from the corridor, and the girls were all so beautiful and graceful. The small dining room was instantly filled with the vibrant air of youth. Each member of the dinner party hugged their good friend, lying on the sofa, leaning on the terrace, irregular jests, irregular actions, made the girls laugh as if they had been electrocuted; and this trembling laughter was precisely what the other party considered pleasure.

People had forgotten that this was the sweltering summer, as if they had fallen into the breath of spring's undulations. The girls' red lips, half-plump lines, were intoxicating the souls of eight young people in the thin cheongsams. Four large dishes were peeking at their ugly behavior in the center of the table, fortunate that they had not been captured. The older chairman had already paid the bill, and they were planning to go to another sleepless world. They swarmed out of the restaurant like a beehive. The cars on the road were filled with people enjoying the breeze, and the water and electric company's chartered cars were interweaving back and forth. Shanghai's sleepless night was beginning at this time; whether it was the sweltering summer, it was like an intoxicated spring.

A seven-story Western-style building loomed before them, with lights shining from every window. Cars and chartered cars were waiting at the entrance for their owners to complete a certain task. The eight young people were swallowed up by the spring in summer.

The Big Casino in Shenzhen, Guangdong 212

— Liang Feng

The Extravagant Gambling Life of Ordinary Wealthy People

The people of Guangdong love to gamble, from big cities to small towns, gambling dens are everywhere, filling the land, all those who have been to Guangdong know that. Amongst all this, the people of Guangdong do not know how much blood and sweat have been extracted from them by those gambling den owners and the local government. This is nothing more than a common phenomenon in Guangdong society. Next to the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway is a place called Shenzhen, that really is an unparalleled large gambling den. Inside this gambling den, there is a very high gambling platform, there is a stage, there are taverns, there are singers (i.e. singing girls), there are female waitresses, in short, all the things a wealthy person

needs to enjoy life are available. Originally, the customers of this casino were mostly rich merchants, politicians, soldiers, and landlords. They used this place as a place for entertainment, throwing away tens of thousands of gold pieces, which was considered nothing at all. From Hong Kong it only takes an hour by train to get to Shenzhen. I once followed a military officer to this place. Inside there were many gambling tables, what roulette big gamble, fan-tan, ti-zhi, really colorful, everything complete. The gamblers bet, at least one dollar, but the daily winnings and losses amounted to ten thousands. These gamblers, some were sixty or seventy years old, some were imposing middle-aged military officers, some were seventeen or eighteen year old youths, some were fat middle-aged wives, some were extremely fashionable girls, some spent all day and all night living there, when hungry the casino boss provided gourmet food, when tired they slept there, those who liked to smoke opium, had female waitresses to accompany them packing it, those who liked to have their bones rubbed, also had hired girls to rub them. So, they really lingered and forgot to return, not caring about wins or losses. What especially caught my attention were those wealthy people's wives and concubines, they gambled even more lavishly, betting millions at a time. I once saw a eighteen or nineteen year old young woman (I heard she was the sixth concubine of a certain important figure in Guangdong), her body was silkily glistening, her fingers were wearing three or four dazzling diamond rings, she brought twenty or thirty thousand dollars, and lost it all in one round, then pawned the ring on her finger for several thousand dollars to bet, she lost it again in a flash, but she remained calm, laughed it off. That kind of situation really made us ordinary poor boys want to avoid her by three houses. You think where do these politicians and wealthy people get so much money to spend on them, isn't it just by squeezing us small ordinary people as much as possible? Alas!

Under the Traffic Lights (40) 214

— Xilin

Li Shiqiao felt ashamed and trembled in his heart when he heard this sentence, and had to ask incidentally:

'How do you know?'

'The front line here also receives newspapers every day. This time, the public opinion is finally united. I see in the newspaper that the boycott of enemy goods this time is really being implemented!'

'If the public opinion in the rear is not united, how can we live up to the soldiers on the front line?' In fact, if Li Shiqiao didn't lie like this, how could he comfort Zhou Shaoping. He followed behind Shaoping, his eyes focused on the fine grass in front of his feet, his hands behind him twisting himself, this seemed to be a close-up in a movie, indicating that the owner of this twisting hand was buried in the troubles of deep thought. Shaoping walked in front, his steps very upright, but sometimes when he encountered stones on the road, he would kick the stone like a ball, flipping it over at least thirty meters. He suddenly turned his face and asked anxiously:

'How is Zhang Honglie? Because I can't go to see him on the front line!' He couldn't get any answer from Shiqiao for a while, and had to shake his head and said; 'It's a pity that he can't come to the front line. Anyone who has charged the enemy will never deny national consciousness again, but since he has been imprisoned 丨Imprisoned by his own compatriots, it only more factually proves the existence and strengthening of class consciousness, and divides the barriers of national consciousness. I feel that for anyone who has no national sentiment, we are going to ask him to go to the front line, and let the enemy's planes and artillery tell him everything.' Li Shiqiao was a person who always liked to theorize, so he was always keen on running publications and making plans. But after he heard Zhou Shaoping's words, he felt that if theory is the expression of words, then how empty and weak it is! Strong theory is brave action, and the action itself is the most powerful theory. Even if he had written more than 100,000 words of papers, had he ever said a sentence as precise as Zhou Shaoping's? He was moved by Shaoping and followed him to the edge of the trench without saying a word. The sentry on the trench asked them to jump into the trench to talk. As soon as Shiqiao jumped into the trench, he smelled a burst of earthy smell, mixed with the pungent smell of sweat. But when the soldiers in the trench suddenly saw Shiqiao in plain clothes, and Shaoping introduced him as representing the XXXXX Federation to comfort the soldiers on the front line, everyone smiled like they had seen their own relatives, some came forward to shake hands with him, and some came to inquire about the situation in the rear. The trench was suddenly filled with a gentle atmosphere. In the sky, soft white clouds floated over like a dream. How fascinating and admirable life is. So, those soldiers with families couldn't help but show a layer of nostalgic wrinkles on their foreheads.

But behind the white clouds, a few enemy planes with gray wings and red circles followed relentlessly, probably to search for the location of our main force.

Immediately, the forward sentries returned to report, the situation was: 'The enemy is about two or three thousand, with a large heavy artillery team, following the cover of the planes, rushing east along Yuexiu Road, the vanguard has reached the old site of the former Shanghai University.

'Go to hell!' Everyone in the trench tightened their armed belts.

The enemy plane circled in the sky and quickly retreated.

Film Special Issue

Preventing Abuse of Actors 215

— Yin Xi

Even animals are protected by organizations. The fact that people are not as good as dogs is sighing. Animals added to the performance in the film have humanitarian organizations who think of protecting them, but actors, being human, are not cared for and protected. Although it is difficult to determine what is so-called cruel to these stars, there are many obvious inhumane things. Even if the stars themselves are willing to endure, I think someone should come forward and advocate for humanity, and should be prohibited or restricted!

It is said that in the movie "The Kid from Spain," there are several scenes of bullfighting performances. Every day when filming, various charitable organizations sent male and female representatives to supervise. They sat from morning to night, for fear that the precious cows transported from Mexico would suffer any abuse or damage. They almost always considered humanitarianism when there were scenes involving animals in the script, so that grace could reach animals. But what about the actors? They don't think about it!

But people should at least have some protection. Are they not even as good as a dog, a cat, or a cow? So it would be best if someone could come out in the future, imitating the method of protecting animals, and organize a "Film Actors Abuse Prevention Association." Probably this association is urgently needed in society.

One day, the Metro Company filmed a dog show in the summer. Because the weather was hot, artificial air conditioning was specially used, and large fans were used to fan the filming site. This way the dogs were very comfortable, because this is what the Animal Abuse Prevention Association advocated. But when Joan Crawford was acting, the weather was just as hot, but she did not enjoy air conditioning. Some people say that even if Joan Crawford suffers some heat, she won't be panting. If she wants to pant, the company will definitely prepare air conditioning for her. This is a joke, but at least it can prove that people's enjoyment is sometimes not as good as a dog!

One day a reporter went to interview a female star named Karen Morley. At that time, Karen Morley was filming three films at the same time, and was very busy. Karen Morley's body has been far inferior to before in recent years. This is probably due to excessive mental and physical labor. When the female reporter entered the room, a doctor held a large syringe in his hand and injected a stimulant into Karen Morley's skin. Karen Morley immediately fainted, like death. The female reporter was so scared that she quickly found a glass of cold water. But she didn't know whether to splash it on Karen Morley's face or pour it into her mouth. While she was hesitating, Karen Morley suddenly woke up, of course with a lot of pain and haggardness on her face, but she still had to stand up and work immediately.

Lang's sacrifice for art is known to everyone. Now his follower Boris Karloff's films such as The Mummy have a great impact on the spirit and body. His makeup takes two hours to complete and one hour to remove. The wax, rosin, paint, and other things used not only cut off his skin's breathing, but also tighten it. This is all harmful to his life. But Boris coveted the celebrity name and the salary of several thousand dollars a week; he disregarded everything. There are many other things like this. Shouldn't we try to think about it from a humanitarian point of view and prohibit or restrict it?

Movie Review

Review of "Bright Moon and Fragrant Quilt" *A Night in Cairo* 216

— Ling He

In the realm of literature, although naturalism has given way to new realism, romanticism still refuses to relinquish its existence. Similarly, while film writers are expected to address reality to some extent in their scripts, their living environment shapes their thoughts and the content of their work. Thus, from different perspectives, they often inaccurately apply real-world themes. To expect them to embrace new realism is generally unlikely. More than that, they remain deeply intoxicated by the sweet dreams of romance and are unwilling to make their audiences frown with the ugliness or horror of reality. This is especially true for the increasingly unstable petit bourgeois class, who are more easily captivated by this dream. As a result, romantic works always garner considerable popularity. Therefore, the production of such films still serves a whitewashing function, which we cannot afford to overlook.

The above explanation is prompted by the content of "Bright Moon and Fragrant Quilt." It is undeniable that this film is pure romance.

Given this, the creators at MGM employed excellent equipment and talent to ensure that this romance would achieve its full potential. The result, of course, not only satisfies them but also pleases the petit bourgeois and the leisure class. That is their success. Clearly, in terms of performance techniques, there is nothing that they cannot boast about. Desert moonlit nights, seductive love songs, a beautiful woman bathing in fragrant water with flower petals scattered, a handsome young man lavishing attention on a beautiful woman, enduring even whipping—all for the sake of capturing a woman's heart, even to the point of heartlessly tormenting her. Playing cat and mouse to the extreme. This reminds us of "Carmen" and "The Soul of the Party." In short, this artist's ideal of love is expressed without reserve in beautiful images. As for the director's meticulousness, the set designer's and cinematographer's skill, and the location shooting, there is no need to point out individual characteristics, nor are there any flaws to criticize.

I believe many are familiar with the great star Ramon Novarro. Not long ago, he played Greta Garbo's lover in "Mata Hari," which we will not forget. He is also adept at portraying foreigners; now, besides Chinese people, he is posing as an Egyptian. His skills were already so exquisite, and he naturally succeeds here as well. However, the female lead, Myrna Loy, deserves even more attention. We saw her in "The Animal Kingdom" with Leslie Howard, where she did not seem particularly successful, but in this film, she has made great progress.

In conclusion, in this film, we can see that MGM, with its vast capital, has reached the pinnacle of performance techniques in all aspects. However, the application of these skills to an empty and unappealing story is still regrettable.

Who Stole Han Shou's Fragrance? 217

— Fu Xi

This story is probably little known even to Rita Hayworth's fans. She had an ounce of perfume, a one-of-a-kind ounce in the world, the crystallization of a chemist's lifetime of effort. This perfume does not yet have a name, so it can only be called the Nameless Perfume. Where did this perfume come from? When Rita Hayworth and Edmund Lowe went to London last year, they met a Parisian perfume maker. This maker had spent many years creating a special perfume, but after all that time, he was only able to extract one ounce. He met Hayworth and gave her the perfume. The method of making the perfume was also destroyed, so Hayworth became the sole owner of this nameless perfume. Now, anyone who visits Hayworth's home can smell a faint fragrance. Hayworth treasures this ounce of perfume as if it were a precious jewel. She says that this extraordinary perfume, even if only a tiny drop is applied to any piece of clothing, will last forever. No matter how it is washed, even if the garment becomes silk brocade, the delicious scent will remain.

Review of "Queen of Atlantis" *Atlantis* 218

— Shen Xiling

I was excited to go to the Nanjing Grand Theater, as this was a work by the famous director (G.W. Pabst), and I had never seen his work before.

A. The Sorrow of the Artist

I recall the Japanese sociologist Hajime Kawakami expressing his sorrow in prison; the German scientist Albert Einstein leaving Germany to join the British nationality; and this change in the style of director G.W. Pabst... Who says that changes in social conditions and the vagaries of political trends do not affect artists, forcing them to submit? Naturally, if G.W. Pabst were a strong person, perhaps this would not have happened; if he is weaker, then only he knows his sorrow—the sorrow of the artist. I only knew him as a progressive director, but today I heard my friend Shusheng say, "He made this film under Hitler's influence and has now gone to France, where he is working on 'Don Quixote'..." The meaning is implicit, and the audience can understand his sorrow. As for whether he is still a progressive director, only his future works can prove it.

B. A Poem of Dreams; A Dream of Poetry; It is...

A French officer, in the hot desert night, recalls his love affair with a desert queen two years prior. Enticed by her seductive charm, he killed a friend and betrayed his comrades, and thus became a fugitive... A slow tempo; the beautiful female lead, like a Venus from Greek sculpture, fully portrays the allure of sexuality. The delicate musical scales will also intoxicate you. Truly a dreamlike poem, or a sweet poem of dreams. But also a cup of fragrant poison. It is enough to assist its master's mission.

C. Reference for Chinese Filmmakers: ...

There are two extremely important flashbacks in this play: the first is at the opening of the play, when the officer Saint-Avon recalls his love affair two years prior. Here, he (the director) does not use Fade-in Fade-out, nor does he use the re-shooting or Dissolve (as in "Spring Dream in the Boudoir"), which we often see in foreign films and consider the best technique. Instead, he uses Cut-in directly, but unlike a direct cut, the first shot of the flashback (several camels moving in the desert) uses a "slow motion" technique, as if imagined. The second flashback in the film is when Handmann recalls that the Queen was originally a singer... Here, he also uses Cut-in directly. However, the important thing is not the shooting technique but the sound effects, which the audience will surely notice. Other aspects, such as the position and angle of the shot changes, can also provide us with considerable reference.

D. Movie knowledge for audiences: ...

Foreign films are not easily welcomed by audiences in mainland China; Chinese films, in order to cater to mainland audiences, cannot use more sophisticated film techniques. These interactions hinder the progress of Chinese cinema. Just as one must learn fractions after learning addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division in arithmetic, there are several places in this film where partial techniques are cleverly applied. For example, the final airplane shadow, footprints in the sand, etc., all save a lot of repetitive narration. Audiences in Shanghai will surely understand, but audiences in the mainland may not. I think it is necessary to bring up these ABCs of film.

New Invention on the Silver Screen: Movies Can Be Shown in the Light 219

Huang Daoheng, a native of Shaozhou, Guangdong, who previously worked at the Sanmin Film Company in this city and has been engaged in the film industry for more than ten years, has invented a method of showing movies in the light. In the past, movies had to be shown in dark theaters, which was detrimental to the health and safety of moviegoers. European and American countries had no method of improving this type of dark cinema. He devoted himself to research and invented a method of showing movies in the light. This method only requires maintaining a certain degree of darkness in the area of the screen, while allowing the audience seats to be exposed to light. There is no need for complete darkness, and windows can be opened for ventilation without affecting the light on the screen. He previously drafted a description and drew diagrams and submitted them to the Ministry of Industry for a patent. After receiving the submission, the Ministry ordered him to bring all the equipment to the Ministry for testing, and the results were very satisfactory. It is now said that this method of showing movies in the light will be publicly demonstrated in Shanghai soon after the Ministry of Industry approves the registration. Dark cinema, which has been around for decades, will be able to open up to the light from now on.

Film Novel: Irish Girl "Peg O' My Heart" (1) 220

— Gu Zhang

Starring Laurette Taylor, produced by MGM. Peg is a young girl from an Irish fishing family. One day, her father, Pant, comes home with Sir Chichester, an English nobleman, who tells her that her grandfather has recently passed away, leaving her a fortune of two million pounds! Peg, now transformed from poor to rich, stares at her father and Sir Chichester in turn, feeling as if she is dreaming. Sir Chichester is waiting to take her to England to inherit her fortune. She turns to look at her father, whose eyes are smiling strangely. Peg takes a long breath, hugs her white dog, and says to it excitedly, "We're rich! You're a rich dog now, too!" Her father also tells her that she doesn't need to catch fish anymore, that catching fish is not befitting of a wealthy young lady, and that she will now live in England.

Peg thinks with a mixture of surprise and joy: England? Her father once told her that English people's feet were almost like cow's feet, cloven-hoofed. England? Her father had said that it was of no use to him, and she didn't know if she would get used to it after she went. Her father told her that her mother was also English. This nobleman, Sir Chichester, is of course also English, Peg thinks, glancing at his feet, which are human feet and not cloven cow's feet. She looks at his face. He looks very honest, with a slight smile, and is also looking at her. She says, "Maybe there are a good person or two over there." Her father tells her to quickly prepare to leave. Peg rushes upstairs, gets halfway up the stairs, and then turns back and calls to her father, saying that she wants to put his clothes in the same box. Her father replies that she should not worry about him, as he is not going with her. When Peg hears that he is not going with her, she rushes back to him and says that she will not go either. Pant and Chichester exchange a look, and Pant tells his daughter that he is just not going with her now. In his heart, however, he is thinking that his daughter will be separated from him forever. She will be living with her aunt, Giggster, and her cousins, Alaric and Iser. He feels reluctant to part with his daughter, but thinking that he is just a poor fisherman, and that a fisherman's life is drifting and uncertain, he truly doesn't know what tomorrow may bring, and who will take care of her if he dies one day. Therefore, he decides to let his beloved daughter inherit the fortune. But he doesn't dare to tell her the truth.

Peg reluctantly puts on her best clothes in a hurry, preparing to leave with Chichester. Before leaving, she reminds her father that he must come, otherwise she will come back. After she runs up the stairs, Chichester says to the old man that he should not deceive his daughter. The old man says that this is the only way to get her to go, and after she leaves, he can have someone write her a letter telling her that he is dead, so she can give up thinking about home. (To be continued)
